---
## \#42 Posted by: chuttney1 Posted at: 2018-12-14T08:00:55.113Z Reads: 571

```
[quote="mishrasubhransu, post:41, topic:77910, full:true"]
Why do you say that? How is it any different than any other DD?
[/quote]
it's been known the performance of a hub motor for eskates is less compared to the motor's can spinning in free air. Regardless of how other companies do their "DD" design, the wheel is an insulator. Makes it hard disperse heat especially when there are no holes like the SK3 motors. It's not bad the motor is fully encased. It's just harder to transfer heat .
```

## \#142 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-03-07T04:35:20.960Z Reads: 345

```
That I can answer my friend. 

Drivetrains (hubs or outrunners) on boards that go for $899 have a fairly standard price point across the industry. 

These drives, and completes, I would expect, to cost $99 more, so $399. 

Make no mistake; they‚Äôre going to get Axial right, and, we‚Äôre going to see a lot of Exway-type decks with all three drivetrain choices (there‚Äôs a drop-through one that looks like an Exway has a baby with a Carbon). 

and to be clear and never start rumors, I am not bound by NDA to Exway nor do I know anyone at Exway.  

After talking it over with a friend, I think that‚Äôs a factory second (axle length) yet this is purely conjecture on our part. 

The sample above does look like it was assembled by a third-party, again just conjecture (my own) but if the parts don‚Äôt meet tolerance Chinese factories don‚Äôt throw things away. Everything is for sale in China, with the right level of connections. 

If I had one, I would most definitely rebuild it, I like that axle. Good luck friends, stoked to see this so early.
```

## \#196 Posted by: BillGordon Posted at: 2019-03-14T12:49:57.131Z Reads: 302

```
Guys, toss away the tissues, put the lotion back on the nightstand and drop your tadgers.

The eLofty DD is legit!

Just came back from my first outing using the notoriously shitty diyeboard ESC (lost all my vescs in two days...doh!), and I'm honestly a bit blown away. The power comes on in a smooth and snappy wave, and it even makes the braking on this crap esc work pretty well. I'm 220 and it has no problem propelling the crap out of my ass.

When I get my Focboxes back, I expect to be an even happier camper.

There's a new discount sheriff in town.
```

The weight of four TB 110s with four eLofty axial motors in a perfect, 50/50 weight distribution sounds ideal.

brakes still feeling good on SF roads? :pray:

update to plan: if the drivetrain they send me works out, we (meaning me) will hire a CNC guru to machine a limited-run of custom SR RKP hangers that are eLofty-compatible, immediately.

## \#288 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-20T05:34:00.029Z Reads: 287

```
My current build is 190KV with 10S4P battery with wheel dia 155mm and gearing ratio 16:50. That gives me a theoretical no load top speed of 190 * 4.2 * 10 * (16/50) * 3.14 * 155 * .000001 * 60 = 75km/hr. Till date, I have used a max of 25Amps/motor.

[case1_esk8_calculator](https://calc.3dservisas.eu/?Rc8xC8IwEAXg_5JZJDFJsa6nOCmBgt1thwjWBjqK_917L0W3765379K3uUs2B_N8zC-z0eKqhd826kU6tbNkUgZKVLtoa_uIysXqxC91CJlOWZDhAUx6y72SujWuJC5BjPKRRLMhf0FDljVpyCfV3pI3rAd4kjVp4rNb9tIMB_J_fxK0W9XYL_wB3BrPF7ghe2XE7IhjGvb5Ag==)

I am planning a similarly capable build using the 75KV elofty with 6x2 pneumatics. I am planning to use 8S5P battery. That would give me a theoretical no load top speed of 75 * 4.2 * 8 * 3.14 * 155 *.000001 * 60 = 73.5km/hr

[case2_esk8_calculator](https://calc.3dservisas.eu/?RY-9DsIwDITfJTNCKUnKz-qiTqBISHSnGYpE2kodEe-O71rK9p3tO9tv85DOnMzrOfRmo-Kqwm1L5UluygdSVAokUdoFaykqqGJuVJGdeQiRheKICAfApLP0jRFVT6IJxCgXiCiWxDWo7WRJarszzrLEO-wenGVJygjfw53jALcn_tdnYRmPpWbiA5hO9eX3TKqbFbHsaM3nCw==)

Using 8S5P gives me the same battery capacity as before, while sagging less. Do people see any potential problem with this new setup?
```

## \#296 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-20T21:02:17.202Z Reads: 296

```
**EDIT: I had mixed up Kv(with unit rpm/volt) and Ke(back emf constant with unit volt/rpm) and so all the analysis here is wrong. Ignore this post**

Your 2 cents are absolutely correct. A little bit of analysis shows that I'll have push about 8 times as much current through the new motors to generate the same amount of torque. The max per motor I consume of my geared pneumatic setup is 25Amps per motor, now to get the same amount of torque it has to be 200Amps per motor. OMG. I wish I had done the calculations before :confused:

So here's the analysis assuming both motors are identical in terms of stator size and magnets.

    Case1: 16:50 geared setup with 190KV
    Case2: DD with 75KV

    KV_1/KV2 = n1/n2 = 190/75 = 2.5333   where n is number of turns in the stator
    torque on wheel1 = 50/16 T1          where T1 is the torque produced by the motor1
    torque on wheel2 = T2                where T2 is the torque produced by the motor2
    T1 = K*n1*A1 & T2 = K*n2*A2          where K is some constant and A is current
    T1/T2 = (n1/n2)*(A1/A2)=2.533*A1/A2

    torque on wheel1 = torque on wheel2  This is what we want
    (50/16) * T1 = T2
    (50/16) * 2.533*A1=**A2= 7.91A1**

The advantage of lower KV is that the motors lets you push higher amps without having to connect to a higher volt battery. Also the resistive losses will be less in a low KV motor(given same copper weight)

@Pedrodemio, @rey8801, @bevilacqua. Does, what I said, seem right? What I am little doubtful is the torque equation( `T1 = K*n1*A1`). I should double check.
```

## \#299 Posted by: bevilacqua Posted at: 2019-03-20T21:26:43.628Z Reads: 292

```
![image|690x260](upload://19bl8aQtAVDi3G7F4Rw56QuNSIw.png) 

(Basic Torque equation for Permag. Syn, Machines)

Psi is the permanent magnet magnetic flux, i the current and p the pole pair. Im not a fan of DD for pneumatic systems, the big downside is the immense current you have to generate for the equal torque as a geared system. How much? well, it depends on the PM-flux, but roughly you multiply the current by the gearing to get to a basic number. 

You will need an immense stator, and high amps to counteract the gearing effect on torque. 

But on the other hand, I get why there is so much interest. If you want to trade some torque and range in benefit of a smoother ride, and also have a simpler (more reliable in many cases) driving solution then go for it :+1:
```

## \#304 Posted by: deltazeta Posted at: 2019-03-20T22:20:09.178Z Reads: 273

```
seems your equation is missing the inductance calculation:
![image|339x60](upload://pyj2qqglDD45At2isKdrAfS1sCd.png)

The psi in the equation is not magnetic flux, but flux linkage. Flux linkage encapsulates the number of turns without explicitly adding it into the equation.
```

## \#311 Posted by: Pedrodemio Posted at: 2019-03-21T00:03:26.918Z Reads: 297

```
Exaclty as @bevilacqua said

What limits us is thermal losses, not how much current the motor can take, that's why Kv doesn't matter for torque production, it only matters when you are building a complete system and have limitations there, in out case maximum voltage and current for battery and esc

(this is all ignoring flux saturation, assuming that we won't saturate the stator)

I think I posted this on the Feather thread, but lets dive a bit.

Lets use my small 5055 motors since they won't touch the current limits of the esc, if I use them at 190 Kv and run them at 40 A I will produce 96W jus of ohmic losses at the windings

Now, since I wanted them to be direct drive I go ahead an rewind them to 95 Kv, while keeping the same cooper fill, really important detail or this doesn't work, this is achieved by doubling the number of turns, but at half the cross sectional area

If I still keeps feeding them the 40 A, my new loss is 192 W, since I know that the original motor at 190Kv @ 40 A already hot, I can't do this, even thought that if my original gear ratio was 2, by keeping the same current in direct drive I will keep close to the same torque, but no equal since we are wasting a lot of power in heat

So we go ahead and reduce the current to 20 A, now we have half the torque as a 2:1 geared setup, while keeping the losses at the same 96 W

What we can take from here is that the is no magic done by rewinding, what dictates the motor performance is Km, which is proportional to motor torque divided to resistive loses, coincidentally you won't find this information anywhere since it would make it obviously that a motor is bad, and other at the same specs is much better

So if we want a direct drive that keeps the same performance as a belt/geared drive, we need to produce the same torque at the wheel at the same losses, basically if we would plot and efficiency graph of the motors they should look the same

We can go further and estimate how big a motor would be

Torque for a given motor can be described as T = K*D¬≤*L, K being a constant for a given motor design, independent of windings, D the diameter and L the length

We will write that as k = T/(D¬≤*L)

I will use my board since I've done this calculations a few times already

I run 40 A at my 6355 motors with a 14:53 gearing in 125mm wheels, that gives me  a motor torque of roughly 2 N.m at the motor and 7.5 N.m at the wheels

The K for this motor design is 9162

Now lets say we will just get this motor and enlarge it to be capable to produce 7.5 N.m at the wheels, so we do T/k = D¬≤*L , lets limits the motor diameter to 85mm to keep a good ground clearance, and doing the calculations we get that our motor should be 128mm long, so a 85128 motor

I think I went too far, hope it's understandable 

But the main point is that gearing allows us to use a smaller motor, and there is not way to get a small motor to perform like a big one. Sure, you could go some crazy cooling, putting dry ice or whatever, running it somewhere that is -70¬∞C, but it will be crazy inefficient, just look at the Raptor 2 and Ghost motors

If you really want to dive deep in this I suggest this book as a starting point, it's a complex topic and I'm nowhere near knowing it well, lots of times I think I have everything figured out and pops another details that makes my head spin

http://www.avislab.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/BrushlessPermanentMagnetMotorDesignVersion2.pdf
```

---
## \#312 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-21T01:28:14.546Z Reads: 279

```
Thanks for the detailed explanation @Pedrodemio. 

**I had stupidly mixed up Kv(with units rpm/volts) and Ke(back emf constant with units volts/rpm)** and totally got confused.  Ke = 1/Kv. Ke is proportional to number of turns and Kv is inversely proportional to number of turns. Now it makes lot more sense. I just need **1.23times more amps to produce the same torque**. That's not too much of an increase in current(not an issue for ESC), but like pedrodemio said, for **same current the ohmic losses would be 2.5 times**(190/75, assuming same amount of copper). For the **same torque the ohmic losses would be 3.8 times**(I^2R loss).  So effectively I would see a decrease in wh/km. Currently I am getting 18wh/km, let's see how much I get with DD. 

    Case1: 16:50 geared setup with 190Kv(rpm/volts)
    Case2: DD with 75Kv(rpm/volts)
    
    Kv2/Kv1 = n1/n2 =75/190 = 0.394      where n is number of turns in the stator
    torque on wheel1 = 50/16 T1          where T1 is the torque produced by the motor1
    torque on wheel2 = T2                where T2 is the torque produced by the motor2
    T1 = K*n1*A1 & T2 = K*n2*A2          where K is some constant and A is current
    T1/T2 = (n1/n2)*(A1/A2)=0.394*A1/A2
    
    torque on wheel1 = torque on wheel2  This is what we want
    (50/16) * T1 = T2
    (50/16) *0.394*A1 = A2 =1.23A1
```

## \#349 Posted by: Sn4pz Posted at: 2019-03-27T15:58:59.497Z Reads: 272

```
[quote="BruSkater, post:345, topic:77910, full:true"]
What‚Äôs the general consensus on airless AT tires? Do you guys like em?
[/quote]

So far the most popular(dont quote me) airless wheel was diyeboards airless one. The downsides were it killed your range as well as limiting your speed, because they would deform at higher speeds.

I would love a solid solution so I dont have to worry about carrying a spare :rofl:
```

## \#436 Posted by: mike.c Posted at: 2019-03-30T10:34:08.744Z Reads: 251

```
Hey, could you elaborate on the noise aspect? Is it a rattle on bad roads? Is it more than what you‚Äôd expect from a usual belt or hub drive? Is there noise from motor bearings?

I have a carbon gt which I tried so much to reduce rattle and the culprit was the wheel bearings. Bones red race bearings just made it worse and the best solution was to clean the original ones and fill them with thick grease. This quietened them heaps but sacrificed free rolling when just spinning the unloaded wheels but it made absolutely no difference to while riding (electric boards don‚Äôt free roll like normal boards anyway so seems pointless for the marginal gains from bearings)
```

## \#445 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-03-30T22:48:58.896Z Reads: 263

```
it will fit, with minor modification (that's the OG Evolve / Avenue hack)

axial motors need clearance on drop-through, and Avenue baseplates are top-mount only so it's a good match

https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/t/no-words-just-pictures-delete-words-2/88821/20?u=topcloud

by the way, the new TB 110 wheels fit perfectly on the eLofty drive. :)

## \#446 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-03-30T22:58:42.174Z Reads: 263

```
maybe one of the options on the group buy can be a pair of pre-modded Avenue base plates for the eLofty hangers.

it should be done at a machine shop.  

one can also drill a hole in the leaf spring to soften it up.

to add to @sofu 's mod, I stopped mine from 'squishing' entirely by placing a hemisphere of 50 Duro [Sorbothane](https://www.sorbothane.com) in the center of the spring:

https://www.amazon.com/Isolate-Sorbothane-Hemisphere-Non-Skid-Durometer/dp/B0084ELFIU?th=1

this sorbothane-in-spring made a big difference in board feel; on long, straight lines, my 90 mm hubs feel like thane.
```

## \#449 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-03-31T03:33:10.611Z Reads: 259

```
the motors are 6850 long / 6700 wide.

With a 67 mm can, I'd definitely stay over 85 mm wheel and suggest a minimum of 100 mm wheel for what we do.

Axles (no wheels) are 308 mm wide, end to end.

Clearance on drop-through flush-mount decks is perfect (as Evolve re-designed for in 2016 with the dropped Carbon GT deck) for 97 MM wheels and up.

With the TB 110 mm wheels, from the top of the baseplate to the ground, is a very speed-bump friendly 125 mm.

Trucks are fully compatible with Evolve DKP base plates, both levels.

The eLofty hangers are wider than the Evolve hangers.

There are few decks that are strong and thin enough to provide the clearance the cans need at full drop-through (non-flush mount, which pushes the deck closer to the motors).  

In fact, I can only think of two: Trampa Orrsum and Loaded Icarus Flex 1 + Alan's enclosure (eboardsperu.com)
```

---

## \#452 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-03-31T04:22:26.446Z Reads: 258

```
I rarely take pics of my work; @sofu 's pic is here: 

before:

https://imgur.com/a/1V2El

after:

https://imgur.com/a/kTBKc

because the Evolve base plate is drop-through, in my opinion, resetting the angle on the Avenue is a task that you do not want to 'eyeball'.  

Even though the Avenue is top-mount, the base plate is non-adjustable (you can't fix it without taking the entire thing out) so after you mess with it a few times if it wobbles - just take it in to a shop.

I placed the sorbothane (hemisphere) underneath the kingpin.
```

## \#453 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-31T05:28:08.923Z Reads: 266

```
[quote="BillGordon, post:173, topic:77910"]
![IMG_20190312_180143.jpg](https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/uploads/db1493/original/3X/9/9/99634ae74a92662c9f8fe5290677670f6f6405ad.jpeg)
[/quote]
The extended shaft version that @BillGordon and @esk8jpn got. 

Unfortunately I got the standard shaft :(  and I am spending time designing wheel hubs to 3D print.

![image|375x500](upload://nnDsnw7nhHtfWJ30Ue6wW0VaHjd.jpeg) 

Guys make sure to ask for the **extended/long axle version**(34mm free shaft length) if you want to use it with the aliexpress 6x2 wheels(I have confirmed this with Kenna). The ones they ship now is 24mm free shaft length by default so suitable for regular skateboard wheel.
```

## \#487 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-04T23:46:37.985Z Reads: 262

```
Printed with some cheap pla at 4 walls and 25% gyroid infill, no cooling. Turned out pretty strong. Apologies for the vertical video.
https://photos.app.goo.gl/5APeedtAqTG9yjRc7

Assembly looks good too.  The wheel has been pressurized to 60PSI for now. I'll push it to 72PSI after a day or so if everything stays in place. Haha. 
![IMG_20190404_194303|375x500](upload://k6HbmHpRMQopmqYXTnh4VbPrYZY.jpeg) ![IMG_20190404_194253|666x500](upload://nzjNI2I7TQUgFnHuVdhVs9svcwl.jpeg) 
![IMG_20190404_194141|666x500](upload://4Zd1ZdNV3urSYzYIfxAaHrqxxFn.jpeg)

Now it's time to print another wheel and ride test it at low speeds only. If all goes well print it in alloy 910(nylon). Since it will bend before it fails, I'll have plenty of warning(in terms of wobbling of the wheel). Printing in alloy 910 will cost me $8 per wheel.  If you are interested in performance of alloy 910, here is a youtube video.  
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8_pt_05BqYk&t=339s
```

## \#501 Posted by: BillGordon Posted at: 2019-04-05T07:36:15.382Z Reads: 265

```
Quick PSA:

I got my 110s, and they look amazing. First rear mounted up with no slop, but second rear had an unacceptable level of slop. But the third wheel I tried had no slop. So don't assume you got all bad or all good wheel cores. Try them all. You only need two proper kegel orientations for 2WD. 

Second, and this is a repeat, but it's kind of crucial: the drives come with the Kegel adapter screws barely fingertight. Blue LT them down, or better yet, use red like I did. I applied, tightened, backed out for an even coat, then back in firm.This has been stated before, but this is not the kind of thing you want to miss.

Ride report forthcoming.
```

---
## \#502 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-06T04:04:44.262Z Reads: 266

```
The files are [here](https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/19o1mDq6L1XR2eg-poi7ln9MzIaLHOELP?usp=sharing) if anyone else wants to print it and give me feedback. 

print setting that I used for test print:
1. 4 walls, bottom layer, top layer. Feel free to increase them. 
2. 0.2mm layer thickness
3. 25%infill gyroid(you should make it 100% for max reliability)
4. Print without cooling fan for max layer adhesion.
5. With supports(20% infill) from the base.
6. Make sure that the flow% is right so that 2 adjacent walls are fused to each other.

![IMG_20190406_000424|666x500](upload://qb0K3rlfcD8zj7nf9VX168X6UyO.jpeg)
```

## \#526 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-07T21:26:27.288Z Reads: 252

```
[quote="Friskies, post:525, topic:77910"]
My thoughts are that the magnets won‚Äôt hold up to the heat over time based on the cost of these drives.
[/quote]
Oh don't be fooled by the cost. 1. They are located in China so prototyping is cheaper and quicker 2. BOM+machining cost is much less than what you imagine 3. Entry into a saturated market means that you mark it lower than your high mark-up competitors. 

As for the magnets, apparently they are rated for 140C, so plenty of leeway. 

Based on my torque requirements, I would produce about 60Watts of heat at max usage. Maybe some motor experts can chime in if that's going to be manageable or not. @Pedrodemio
```

---
## \#527 Posted by: Pedrodemio Posted at: 2019-04-07T21:37:48.010Z Reads: 249

```
I have no idea how much heat a motor can dissipate

There are so many parameters that it‚Äôs hard to make a prediction 

Best way I can suggest is to test, pick a demanding route, do it in a consistent way riding and weather wise and log everything with Metr or similar 

In my limited real world experience with different motors, the peak amp doesn‚Äôt matter, if your motor is overheating, lowering the current won‚Äôt help much unless your riding style really makes use of the extra punch

Example, my dual 5055 took the same time to overheat at 40A and at 20A, this means the motor is undersized for my riding style and terrain
```

## \#536 Posted by: goldrabe Posted at: 2019-04-07T23:19:58.705Z Reads: 258

```
Yes I learned that the hard way, this is a Metr. log from Enertions R-Spec silver motors, I tried to lower battery amps from a total of 60A to 50A and motor amps from 80A to 50A to avoid heat and get better efficiency. To my surprise even with the  new Beta value the motors reached 100¬∞C in the same distance of my ride.\
https://metr.at/r/TAWof
Here is a example of a 6364 based hub motor which I guess is similar in design then the elofty drive, sadly it has no temp sensor but the motors are hand warm after the complete ride whereas the R-Spec hubs will be at 120¬∞C.\
https://metr.at/r/B2Vyp
```

## \#538 Posted by: Pedrodemio Posted at: 2019-04-07T23:28:01.475Z Reads: 252

```
Nice to see that, just be careful, the motor may be warm at the outside but cooking on the windings

Main problem is that people go from a running a belt (or whatever) setup with 60A and change to a hub and keep the 60A when it should be much lower, at that current a lot of your energy is going into heat and probably saturating the motors pretty bad, more heat

If you have time try them with something like 20A each motor, keep the battery at the same or 40A total

Does anyone have a Raptor 2 and can share the default current settings? My guess they are pretty low
```

## \#540 Posted by: goldrabe Posted at: 2019-04-07T23:37:03.390Z Reads: 246

```
They recommend 30A battery amps for each motor and 60A -60A, I am already lower than that.\
I used the 6364 motors more than one year without issues, I don't think that they are cooking. 
I took them apart to check the inside and no loose magnets or melted windings.\
The only variable is the controllers and firmware. VESC6 with Ackmaniac on 6364 and Unity on the R-Spec motors.

## \#554 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-04-09T06:42:56.862Z Reads: 265

```
presuming @marcmt88's innovation works, I hope to see these out there soon :) 

Janux Quattros are certainly not as inexpensive as a POM adapter for a Haggy wheel, yet these are undeniably the best wheels in the world available today for the TorqueBoards Direct Drive and eLofty Direct Drive.  

Janux Quattros are smaller than factory Evolve AT wheels, yet interestingly, Evolve designed and even manufactured a 150MM that was never sold and we think abandoned for the MBS deal; @okp has actually seen the Evolve 150s, and of course he has, because he is legend.

Quattro 150s can run Bergmeister tires for clearance or trade-up to the wider, heavy-duty Chinesk8 '6x2' never-flat tire.  150MM on RKP/TKP needs no introduction by me; that's every Shooter build ever.

Makes me think this gen2 Carbon that we're all contributing towards just might board feel among the finest Evolves ever made, bar none - if not the best, ever, by returning the Gen 2 Carbon to 150 mm.  

Quite an accomplishment for the community, if you consider it.  Tesla did the same thing with a Lotus.  Give yourselves a pat on the back. :) 

Now, we stay tuned for @sofu's test... with Marc's new Quattros for Direct Drive and TorqueBoards 110s.

## \#569 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-04-10T00:57:52.099Z Reads: 265

```
https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/uploads/db1493/optimized/3X/2/7/272905d71364748a23a558658960c0fe825e37f6_2_1332x1000.jpeg

this is the custom Avenue hanger @donta42 made for Avenue RKP base plates, with the Sorbothane hemisphere that eliminates almost all vibration, that I described earlier.

as we're delivering the Evolvelofty to @sofu on Thursday :stuck_out_tongue_winking_eye: we will also be testing one prototype CNC Quattro wheel, and if it works, you just may see Janux Quattro DD's added to our group buy. 

We are presently considering one more innovation; we are considering a CNC hanger to adapt the eLofty motors and Janux Quattro DDs to one of two, leading RKP base plates:

* Surf Rodz RKP-compatible hangers, motor and traditional.  Note: tall SR RKP adjustable base plates will be highly recommended to provide clearance for the eLofty motors, @sender is working on these.

* Caliber II-compatible hangers, motor and traditional.  Note: @rey8801's Hammock adjustable base plate will be highly recommended for the eLofty motors (I ordered two).

If we can get your guidance on Caliber or Surf Rodz RKP, I think we can finalize scope, get to production and make these wheels and RKP hangers real, show Reddit that our community can deliver the goods.

We won't be the first to bring axial drives to RKP, but we will be the best.
```

## \#572 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-10T05:07:54.463Z Reads: 260

```
So I couldn't resist and went for a ride outside with nrf51_vesc installed. It now connects to the vesc_tool, turns out my phone needed a restart. **Look at the wh/km** :smiley: . I almost came back to where I started from.  I was pretty surprised and thought maybe I have the wheel diameter wrong, but no, it's 155mm with gearing ratio 1:1 as it should be. I video recorded a small part of the ride and is linked at the bottom.

As for steep hill climbing, it climbed the hardest hill nearby, albeit at a lower speed. It is understandable because I currently have a 5S battery. Climbing needs current draw and that leads to sag. Now imagine the sag on top of 5S battery. 

@janpom,I was riding at around 30km/hr and didn't feel any wobble.     
![image|281x500,80%](upload://t13dGejsqWVVV6rxI3LEBziPVdL.png)
![image|281x500,80%](upload://acALwuQ3CSYLXGsOWymOB6VwaGM.png)
![image|281x500,80%](upload://4F3FGt2jedNEy93ORykdHMgbMow.png) 

At the end of the ride the 1st wheel lost it's tire holding ring as it went over the cobbled stone speed bumps. Finally! I am impressed that a PLA prototype with 25% infill lasted as long as it did. The other wheel that has more walls and top layers hasn't fallen apart yet. I want to see how PETG will fare at those settings before I finally print Nylon. I can probably print at 100% infill and be done with it. Will probably cost be a couple of dollars more. 
![image|666x500](upload://taTMsOMAKkZffhlx4B6SCxjj73O.jpeg) 
![image|375x500,88%](upload://d9VnUBkEgTNKwdBmqNQJ8GQRWCZ.jpeg) 
![image|375x500, 88%](upload://vff0fh47IZEPKQWTT6QIfwHb27L.jpeg)   
Right wheel and Left wheel

https://photos.app.goo.gl/11er3K2C6PatomEA9
```

## \#608 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-04-10T17:52:22.532Z Reads: 264

```
No affiliation with Miles and I‚Äôve only seen them on Craigslist ;)  

Remember how I said this is the year China gets axial direct drive right. We‚Äôre going to see more of these. Looks like by Summer now, which is awesome. 

Boosted was widely copied in gen 1, right. 

This year, Evolve, BajaBoard, MBS and Trampa copies are all in production at different plants in mainland China. 

These are all esk8; I believe the carbon fiber-print MBS deck is on eBay now. Vic Duan of Verreal posted a video recently with the BajaBoard copy. The Trampa copy is the same Chinesk8 channel truck esk8 kit we see on DIY, paired with a black wooden deck that looks like a Kheo and those Sunmate FakerStars. 

My opinion, the only one that‚Äôs ‚Äògood‚Äô is the Evolve with axial, because that‚Äôs an actual step-up from Evolve today in every way (power, maintenance, quiet, trucks are better). 

I think we can expect to see a few Bamboo GT clones from a few SIs this year, each with their own flavor of components. The carbon decks floating around are either genuine Evolve OEM or what they call ‚ÄúCarbon Evo‚Äù which is a Carbon GT knockoff that has rounded kicks, like a dance board (I don‚Äôt like it). 

The latter deck will be offered by 3-4 manufacturers in a $1599 complete.

So, are the parts in that pic the same as the eLofty?  Maybe. Those look like my motors which have already been replaced. 

Enclosure is real cf, deck is supposedly even better than Evolve‚Äôs. I like these DKP trucks better than the real thing. 

I am amazed that board could be bought for so little with 10S4P 30q - I would think $700 is manufacturer cost. Please post a link, happy to talk with them about bringing in 10+ for the group buy (we‚Äôd part them out at cost).
```

## \#613 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-11T02:29:06.984Z Reads: 255

```
Average speed was pretty low, maybe around 20km/hr. I was very wary of the 3D printed wheels breaking. Haha. And it did, but fortunately not in a way that it would throw me off the road.

So what I suspect the reason for the insanely low wh/km is low rolling friction. For my ride I initially went uphill and then downhill. The downhill part I didn't have to apply any throttle. If it were my belt drive I would have to apply some throttle to ensure that it kept moving at a decent speed.
```

## \#633 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-12T08:40:30.365Z Reads: 264

```
So the mystery of lost wh/km is **somewhat** solved. I just did a complete loop that GPS tells me was 3.37km but the vesc odometry says 4.862 km.  

The **incorrect** consumption((wh_out - wh_in)/dist) is reported to be **7.8Wh/km**=((39.87-2.14)/4.862).   
The **correct** consumption can be calculated as: (39.87-2.14)3.37 = **11.19Wh/km**. This is why I said **"somewhat"** earlier. It is still pretty low, given I am using half penumatics. Haha. 

The corrected average speed is 3.37km/9.75min = 3.37km/0.1625hr = 20km/hr  

The one variable which I didn't take into account is the **number of magnets**. I just said "yes" to the default value of **14 magnets** during VESC setup but maybe that's wrong. 14magnets*4.862/3.37=20.2magnets. So I guess eLofty has **20 magnets** or 10pole pairs. I'll ask Kenna if that's true.

**EDIT: Kenna replied that it 18.** Either the tire diameter in VESC is a bit more or the GPS underestimates the distance a bit because it measure in a straight line(even though you are carving)

![image|281x500](upload://xt8g84ANNmJ5SjDF37lD0cB6K6a.png) 
![Screenshot_20190412-041236|281x500](upload://gOej9mRYebm9jZX41YxILsoGTWK.png)
![IMG_20190412_044245|666x500](upload://crOVPgsfzpwAIHfGzi6Td4vLANw.jpeg)

@goldrabe
```

## \#643 Posted by: marcmt88 Posted at: 2019-04-12T14:57:33.704Z Reads: 251

```
Generally, Acetal Delrin (POM) is typically 3-4x more expensive than aluminum especially with larger stock.  The cost is offset by machining time which typically takes half the time to cnc aluminum.  Price wise, parts made out of POM is ~10 to 20% cheaper than aluminum.
```

---

I‚Äôm probably not adding anything you haven‚Äôt found already but just in case, In the ‚Äúfocbox unity support...‚Äù thread there a long conversation about throttle curves starting at like post 33.

In post 53 @trampa  explains why he cosiders changing the pos/neg ramp time settings or other options better than messing with the throttle curve. Then they elaborate on this in the following threads.

I think I‚Äôve seen someone mention a trim nob on that remote that you could try to adjust.

Anyways I‚Äôm sure I‚Äôm not saying you haven‚Äôt considered, but thought I‚Äôd throw that out there
```

---
## \#664 Posted by: pat.speed Posted at: 2019-04-13T12:51:54.851Z Reads: 247

```
Don‚Äôt play with the trim. That adjusts the neutral dead band position. If turn the board will hold that speed constantly without you finger moving the trigger, turn it the other way and the brakes will be applied until you either turn it back or pull the throttle a little to reach the dead band again.

Works great for a poor mans cruise control
```

## \#697 Posted by: Winfly Posted at: 2019-04-14T08:05:47.593Z Reads: 240

```
Can't say too much about Elofty drives yet. The battery we put on the Gen2 deck somehow died and the metr stopped working in pretty early in the ride. With the setup we had, all I can say is it has good very torque and once you tuned the throttle curve, the acceleration is good. But for braking you can brake hard down to some rolling speed (maybe 5mph). And then you basically have no brake. Not sure it's the unity or inherent design of the drives. I don't have this issue with hummies on FOCBOXes and 6.6s.

## \#700 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-14T08:21:49.864Z Reads: 250

```
[quote="mishrasubhransu, post:572, topic:77910"]
As for steep hill climbing, it climbed the hardest hill nearby, albeit at a lower speed. It is understandable because I currently have a 5S battery. Climbing needs current draw and that leads to sag. Now imagine the sag on top of 5S battery.
[/quote]

I had taken this video the very first day I put on those PLA 3D printed wheels. From the video I don't know if you can see or not how steep the slope is. It climbed that on **155mm wheels on 5S battery**. Now that should give one a sense of torque at 10S. So I don't know how much more torque does one expect from non-geared motors. It can easily handle 110mm. Of course the equation changes when someone is significantly heavier(I weigh 76kg)

The noise is coming from the front MBS wheels on brick path.

https://photos.app.goo.gl/FiZeNquJNhCBr4yX8
```

## \#701 Posted by: rey8801 Posted at: 2019-04-14T08:41:59.404Z Reads: 249

```
Man don't get me wrong, but as me and others we have a different taste for torque. To better understand I search a torque capable of through you off above 40kmh if you don't balance well your weight. I am sure they bring you from A to B, that's fine. What I think @brenternet meant is that when he gave the full throttle the response didn't give him the feeling he was looking for. I can understand. I also made a DD mad Fury using 75Kv and they are really strong with 90mm, now I use 97mm wheels and they are still plenty strong, but I also said to people who will go them that probably are really nice up to 100mm wheels. Not because they won't move the board but because they won't be able to deliver the same torque. Thsts why I am now testing new 60Kv motor for AT set up. It's all about what you need.
```

## \#715 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-04-14T14:43:02.348Z Reads: 261

```
Most of all, I want to thank @sofu, @Winfly and all BAESK8 for driving this invaluable test, for all of us.  

We tried this last year with the Metasurf drives and let's just say when I heard @FranciscoV and @Touch415 posting on Facebook that the axles were bending on our test units lol, the first thing I thought was: someone is going to read this, and save themselves from injury and that's awesome.  That's what it's all about, the science.

This year, it's eLofty science.  Huge major difference: Ownboard means scale and that's a more real-world reason to ask @Deodand to check this out for us on the Enertion FOCBOX Unity.  

It's all stoked, I think this new crop of axial drives (and the 6868 outrunner motors) will drive new people to DIY like it did for Evolve owners who sought their first battery upgrades.  Unity could be ready for folks who want more out of their Ownboard Carbons.  @marcmt88's wheels will be ready for Ownboard Carbons.  Easy to imagine a picture of that Ownboard Carbon wearing Janux Quattros all over Instagram.

Again, huge heartfelt thanks to @sofu, @Winfly for always pushing the envelope, to @BillGordon and @DAddYE for finding these things in the first place and to @Touch415 and @FranciscoV for always keeping it real.  Love you guys, mean it
```

## \#733 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-04-14T18:21:00.163Z Reads: 259

```
[quote="ryansinatra, post:717, topic:77910"]
So, when‚Äôs the group buy? :smile:
[/quote]

Quick update:

On the ESC front, I reached out to Kenna this morning with an update that Sofu is working with Jeff on the Unity.  Ownboard will ship and this provides us the opportunity to see how their Hobbywing ESC performs. 

On the wheel side, I think here in the Bay Area, modestly speaking, we have every Kegel wheel on the market to test against TB and eLofty.  I feel confident the right equasion will be solved.  @BillGordon is discussing the potential to source larger, 100 MM wheels (we understand wheels take time, yet another source than Labeda would be great).  They are testing 200 MM pneumatics and airless, and my opinion, I think they will stick to the baconator wheels because they are cheaper and faster to produce than urethane.


![image|666x500](upload://dC6m7ku4LsUBbzU0E6XXKMBM4Jd.jpeg) 

Finally, on drivetrain, we will see another motor change.  This is purely conjecture on my side, but I think it will be the larger 6368 silver motors that @Tetsu posted (and by the way dude, you rock for going in and visiting with Ownboard, thank you and @esk8jpn for all the eLofty/ownboard love).

Makes me wonder if we do a group buy today, will we be looking to replace our parts in two months for those bigger motors. 

I think Sofu's review with a working battery and brakes will tell us what to do, next.  

update: we also have a standing order for the new, larger motors to ship as soon as they're available.  

The "Master Plan(tm)", in full disclosure, is to ask @marcmt88 for a work order to prototype a Caliber II hanger that we can put the bigger eLofty motors on, underneath @rey8801's Hammock baseplate.  

Pretty sure that is the best "open source Carvon" recipe that we can come up with.  Knowing Ownboard and a couple more unnanounced brands are working with eLofty gives me comfort the platform will be around, DD won't be a niche option anymore.
```

## \#740 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-14T19:16:52.213Z Reads: 245

```
[quote="Touch415, post:719, topic:77910"]
I remember hummie hubs were semi hot and the enertion hubs were more hot
[/quote]
What are the wheel sizes for hummie and enertion? The eLofty was paired with 110mm wheels, right?

Going up a hill current will be proportional to wheel size(after you remove the wind drag and other dissipative forces) and heat is proportional to square of current. @Touch415  I hope you can see the flaw in your comparison. 

I would love to see apples being compared to apples. Like TB 75KV to eLofty 75KV with 110mm wheels.

## \#754 Posted by: Bundymus Posted at: 2019-04-14T20:20:33.487Z Reads: 237

```
I'd like to chime in with my own anecdote on direct drives in regards to braking and heat.  I haven't tested my new TB DD on the 12S built yet but do have the Carvon XLs (85kv) running 107mm on a 10S running dual focboxes setup.  Braking at speed is fine but does get weaker as the board slows down forcing you to mostly foot brake to stop.  My experience echos @rey8801 where it seems 97-100mm wheels are the sweet spot for 75kv DDs because I had the same experience with the Carvon Exo motors as well.  In regards to heat, the larger motor on the XLs fare a bit better than the Exos.  The XLs get fairly hot too after a good ride on mixed elevations.  I'm beginning to think this behavior is something that is a quirk with all DD in general and you might need to enable reverse in order to achieve full braking for heavier riders and when running big wheels.
```

---
## \#755 Posted by: rey8801 Posted at: 2019-04-14T20:29:30.308Z Reads: 237

```
I think it comes down to the lower rolling resistance of these motors. Mine even without weight start to roll with the minor slope. it really almost feels as a normal skate wheels with a bad bearing let say. Of course is not the same as a normal free wheels but it's the closet I got so far. Probably the normal drag from belt motor helps at really low speed where regenerative braking are inefficient.
```

Not sure if that fix applies to the weak braking as the board slows down in the case of direct drives.

## \#789 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-15T23:32:08.187Z Reads: 247

```
@Hummie, well **elofty is 0.087ohm@75RPM/V** so why are you surprised that **wowgo is  0.190ohm@56RPM/V**? It just means they use less copper than eLofty. It's kind of evident from their wattage rating of 350W continuous and 1000W peak.

## \#792 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-16T00:42:02.615Z Reads: 256

```
Here is a realtime plot for eLofty. Kenna said they use  20 magnets(10 pairs) so that can be used to find the KV.

rpm/volt = (erpm/pole_pair)/(volts\*duty_cycle) = (9597/10)/(19\*0.95) = 53.16KV. Well, so these are ~55KV not 75 as advertised.   

@rey8801, what resistance are you getting on the mad hubs(and yours) dd? and what's the KV for that one? 
![image|690x360](upload://bNxAdBXBkkKKOSvpga454dG8y96.png)
![image|318x361](upload://eUoQaJep0f8dNQpL8jUEBIAjOZC.png)

## \#812 Posted by: Lucifer Posted at: 2019-04-16T13:01:42.689Z Reads: 252

```
[quote="hiboute, post:809, topic:77910"]
she sent me a photo of a hairdrier
[/quote]
:sunglasses:

Behind the main 12mm nut that keeps the motor in place, there is a very thin other nut that looks like a 13mm washer, maybe 2mm thick. I thought it was part of the main axle at first. Scrap away all the glue you can, then use a very thin lubricant, find very sharp pliers, and try to unscrew the ununscrewable... It helps to go back and forth rotating the nut to help getting all the glue residue out of the thread.
```

## \#856 Posted by: Friskies Posted at: 2019-04-18T14:06:56.058Z Reads: 247

```
I have a friend with TB DD and an extra Metr unit that we can throw in next ride but I can tell you right now that weak low speed braking affects all direct drives. You will be able to minimise it by running a 4x4 setup but I am yet to try a set of motors that isn't affected by this. I have Carvon SDV4 as well as hummies and access to TB. So far the only set with nice strong breaks at low speeds are hummies (yes I know they are not DD - insert DD argument). My friend with the TB DD has to foot brake on steep hill stops where as on the hummies I more or less come to a complete stop on significantly lower brake settings (too much for him will lead to wheel lock up at higher speeds). As for the Carvon drives they are in 4x4 config but am waiting on the deck to see the results there, I'm pretty sure they are 115KV so its not much point trying to compare them in 2WD.

You have to remember here that a lot of people want torque. It gets you out of messes, gives you better brakes and in general is more fun. There is not point having a top speed of 80kmh if it takes you 10 minutes to get there if you catch my drift. In saying that these drives do offer a lot for their price and that is something that is good to remember. If someone was on a budget and could only afford $xxx and did not want belts then these may be an option. In their current form though DKP is kindof useless. They don't really accelerate by the looks of it and even if they could do 50kmh they would be a death trap until the RKP version is available. 

Quality really is in the eyes of the beholder. For me it needs to be fast, have good torque, stable, durable and most importantly reliable. The speed and power come from high grade magnets which I'm almost sure that these drives do not run, stability is not there as they are designed for DKP and as for durability and reliability only time will tell. I'm not trying to neg them here but for that price you need to make sacrifices. Its not impossible for someone to make some amazing drives and sell them for no margin or below cost but this is China we are talking about.
```

## \#861 Posted by: Friskies Posted at: 2019-04-18T17:06:33.741Z Reads: 249

```
Between my friend and I we have about 4 meepo hub sets. They were good for the price but the moment you get on the hummies you realize that they are just worlds apart, I consistently have members in group rides astounded at how easily I keep up and even outperform some of their setups. All motors will get hot (you can make any motors hot enough by just running continuous high amps through them) so it becomes how much heat they handle heat before irreparable damage. The weakest part heat wise in most motors are the magnets. If you get the best quality magnets you will get higher power and higher heat thresholds. I know there is a lot more that goes into motors than that in regards to maintaining magnetic fields et. Speak to @Hummie about it - he is honestly a genius and will tell you how much parts actually cost lol.

@evoheyax sums up quality motors pretty well .

[quote="evoheyax, post:653, topic:25251, full:true"]
We recommend 12s for these hubs. I‚Äôm sure you could do much higher also, theres nothing really stopping you.

1500 watts per motor in 4wd is where I start to lose traction on hard accelerations, so if you really need every little bit of power, theres always that option.

In terms of how much power these motors can take, it‚Äôs really unknown at this point. I think 1500w con is a conservative number.

At the end of the day, what makes a motor powerful and to be able to handle high current and high amps:

* Small air gap (check)
* Large stator (check)
* Lots of copper (check)
* Big and powerful magnets (check)
* Ultra low winding resistance (check)
* High heat components in case things do get hot under high loads (check)

In terms of size, these are larger than most outrunner motors. Bigger stator, more copper, and a lower winding resistance. Everything in the motor is rated to at least 300 F, most parts are rated to 400 F, though I wouldn‚Äôt recommend getting them close to there. If you really want the power, 4wd is a better way to go anyways. Don‚Äôt think the focbox or any vesc can reliably do 80a con anyway. You do less stress on the motors and esc‚Äôs also. I think 3000w con is more than enough for most who want a dual drive hub motor. That‚Äôs 10x the power output of those cheaper china hub motors.

The only outrunners I expect will beat these hub motors will be 80mm outrunners. Those guys have a much larger stator, larger magents, ect, and a hub motor made for air filled tires would be the only way you could compete with those things. Even then, I beat Dereks 80mm motors off the line 3/3 times. Only time will tell!
[/quote]

PS: I think you have edited your last post at least 5 times now @mishrasubhransu
```

## \#875 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-19T03:49:09.444Z Reads: 253

```
Umm, really? Say you have identical motors and have 2 setups. 
1. 2wd with 83mm wheels, with Kv
2. 4wd with 166mm wheels, with Kv

Simple math tells me that both of these setups can produce equal force, but the i^2R losses will be doubled in the second case. However, since they are distributed over 4 motors(and not 2) so motors in both the setups will heat up equally when each setup produces the same force. 

So they wouldn't heat up more. Am I wrong somewhere?

---------------------------------------
Now if we consider the case below(same size but different Kv), I have an intuition that both setups will be equivalent in terms of heat production and force production. But math has to worked out to say for sure.
1. 2wd with 83mm wheels, with Kv
2. 4wd with 166mm wheels, with Kv/2
```

---
## \#876 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2019-04-19T04:00:02.070Z Reads: 244

```
A lot really does depend on the motor itself and what it's built with. It's hard to generalize too much.

They may be capable of producing the same torque, but what your forgetting is how that torque is applied. The bigger wheel has a longer distance between the stator teeth and magnets (where the torque is being created) and the contact surface of the wheel.

It's like trying to close a door by pushing the hing side of a door vs pushing the handle side. Your proposing a linear increase in torque when in fact you need a quadratic.

You can change the kv, and it will help, but it's not equivalent to using a larger diameter stator. This is why even Dexter himself said the current DD's with pnuematics is not a permanent solution.
```

---

In case you misunderstood me, I'll say one thing though: notice that I didn't use the word "torque", but rather force. Where Tau=f*r

## \#880 Posted by: Lucifer Posted at: 2019-04-19T09:34:27.223Z Reads: 253

```
[quote="mishrasubhransu, post:875, topic:77910"]
Now if we consider the case below(same size but different Kv), I have an intuition that both setups will be equivalent in terms of heat production and force production. But math has to worked out to say for sure.

1. 2wd with 83mm wheels, with Kv
2. 4wd with 166mm wheels, with Kv/2
[/quote]

Assuming your motors have a constant efficiency over the whole rpm range, that's correct, however this example is misleading. @evoheyax is talking about "motors getting too hot" and here you imply same heat production but overlook heat dissipation, which doubles in your 4WD case.

Another way to see it is "you'll get at the same speed with both setups with the same battery, but second case will keep cooler motors". 
But no matter how you phrase it there will always be side cases where equivalent setups become better or worse, mostly because the temperature depends on :

1. heat dissipation which is function of surface, speed, and a small correction factor k*rpm 

2. other thermal factors that will systematically be overlooked as thermal conductivity of the truck/axle/bearings/connection to the wheel, and heat capacity of all these elements you're slowly cooking - that is likely a happy mix of various metals and thermoplastic polymers covered by a fine dust or a heavy mud layer :-D
```

---

here you imply same heat production but overlook heat dissipation, which doubles in your 4WD case.
[/quote]

Finally. Someone who understands. Yep, you are right. The 4WD will actually run cooler because it has more surface area & heat sinking mass. 

When you say misleading, it's quite the opposite. Isn't it? I was making a case for 4WD and didn't show everything that's in favour. :smiley: 

[quote="Lucifer, post:880, topic:77910"]

## \#892 Posted by: Lucifer Posted at: 2019-04-20T08:45:35.509Z Reads: 256

```
Then it's more of a VESC firmware issue. What you describe is a normal effect that any motor will show to some extent, for instance if you short the phases of a running motor you'll get less and less counter-torque as the rpm goes down. It doesnt matter if you have gears or a belt drive system, because the motor is still turning fast enough until you reach a speed low enough to consider that you can step on the ground. But if you turn it slowly enough, any shorted motor will become extremely easy to rotate.

So what you need in order to get a more or less linear decceleration until you stop is to have the VESC shift from regenerative braking to active braking (what is the VESC "backwards mode") under a pre-set rpm (typically when you switch to sensored mode) but you want to backwards mode to stop before you actually start moving backwards. Ideally the VESC would then shift to an active "stationary mode", keeping a low current flowing to stabilize the wheels in a fixed position until you release the remote's brake. This is the same kind of modification that has been implemented on Ackmaniac's firmware version, but with a slightly different algorithm.
This would be a super cool feature actually.. 
Couldn't anyone just find a way to blackmail Ackmaniac or something? :yum:
```

---

## \#904 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-04-21T01:05:38.937Z Reads: 248

```
So it works fairly well. I set the min eRPM to  -500 and so I can still brake hard on a downward slope and have it stop immediately but after stopping it starts climbing back at a very slow pace. Of course this is if you are not paying attention. If you are paying attention, you just let go off the trigger when it first comes to stop. 

Ideally I would like it to not go backward so I set the erpm to -100 and it made bad cogging sound. So I prefer -500eRPM to -100eRPM.
```

---

## \#939 Posted by: BillGordon Posted at: 2019-04-24T06:31:29.611Z Reads: 239

```
I have run them on a 10s2p Meepo Sanyo and a few LingYi ESC variants and it amounted to a substantial upgrade over budget board hubs. Perfectly happy with them in that application, in fact. 

Not sure how the HW ESC will fare, but should be OK as @topcloud says.

For wheels, if you can find a set of 100mm Boa Constrictors, they would be ideal from a clearance standpoint without losing too much torque. 

The DDs will also offer increased performance later if you upgrade to a bigger battery and VESC.
```

## \#976 Posted by: Schtekarsten Posted at: 2019-04-26T02:09:51.039Z Reads: 254

```
I would be a bit cautious about the anti-spark though. The good thing (well is it?) is that you might be able to bypass the anti-spark module and all its functions, and use a good old loopkey or a properly designed anti-spark module.
but sure they have dubbled the mosfets and put them in parallell compared to the regular dual 4.20, so it will be very capable current wise.
not sure about the SMD soldered caps either, have heard mixed thoughts regarding vibration. so you might have to end up securing them with some silicone.

Flipsky sent over two units for me and @Gamer43 to test out so more on that will come, might take a little while though as the package is still in china and I'm balls deep in other stuff
```

```
Group buy update.

Pricing is almost final; big thanks to @Winfly and Kenna at Lofty for hammering it out.

We're doing this 'group buy' a little differently; we've pre-negotiated a volume discount for you all, with direct purchase and direct fufillment.  No delays between you and your stuff.

This means the buyer will simply order and pay Lofty directly via Kenna, and, you'll receive your product directly from Lofty, just like magic. :woman_mage:  We'll ask any other participating vendor to do the same.

Finally, in full disclosure, there is no markup, rebate, eval units or anything on the back-end of this deal.  We're buying at the same price as everyone else, of course.  One tribe.

Lofty is a 'prosumer' level product so please don't expect Carvon SDR or TB DD.  One bundle we're putting together is to help Meepo, Ownboard, etc. owners replace their hubs with axials.  Lofty's 90 MM Loftythane is simply in another dimension when compared to any 90 MM hub drivetrain.

We'll make a new thread and post it tomorrow, hopefully with our team discount and a Google signup sheet, so Kenna can reach buyers directly.

Thanks team :)

## \#1022 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-04-27T17:54:45.296Z Reads: 247

```
Team,

After many hours of negotiations, @Winfly has successfully negotiated community discounts with Lofty Shenzhen, for all our builders.  Thank you, Wing and Kenna.  In summary:

* We have tiered pricing; the more the community buys, the less we all pay;
* We will start at (30) qty. pricing for the forum (thank you Kenna);
* If we go past (30) paid orders, you will receive a credit from Lofty for the difference towards any other item in the builder's catalog;
* Orders will be placed directly with Lofty;
* Payments will be sent directly to Lofty, and;
* Prices include shipping to your door from (you guessed it) from Lofty. :slight_smile:
* If the quality is good, we will repeat this offer every 3 months.

New-in: **P-MODS**.  Lofty makes batteries and offered 4p and 5p configs; instead, **we asked Lofty to build us **P modules** that all builders could stitch together and use in all enclosures.**  Project lead: @Winfly 

Sourcing quality, durable "P-Modules" is our next priority, to help all builders.

Next-up: **LUNAR 100 MMs**.  Lofty can get a mould made up based on their 90 MM Kegel wheel, which is outstanding in quality and juice.  Look for our review of the 90 MMs soon.

We are waiting on pricing for these wheels.  Wheels will have significant up-front costs, so lead @topcloud 

**We're closing this deal and committing to Lofty :)** with great thanks to the other two manufacturers that reached out.  We will be organizing more of these in the very near future.

1. We'll post a builder's catalog with builder's tiered pricing; you all will get to see the tiers; 
2. Buyers fill out a form selecting what they'd like, add contact infomation, and;
3. Kenna reaches out to you directly, to process your orders.  Everything ships immediately DHL.

Be back tomorrow.  Safe riding today.

**EDIT: if any manufacturer has a deck they'd like to drop-in to this Builder's Buy at a 15-25% discount, please let us know.**
```

## \#1059 Posted by: topcloud Posted at: 2019-04-29T14:25:25.951Z Reads: 275

```
friends: awaiting confirmation on our starting position in the Indie Builder's discount; will update today.

Here's an example of what to expect:

**Lofty 2WD Double Kingpin Direct-Drive, front and rear DKP trucks (complete) with Lofty 90 MM Stratus wheels:**

* Retail 2019: **$499** (DKP drivetrain, F/R, with wheels)
* Direct from Lofty, on eBay, with shipping included: **$459 shipped direct (right now)**
* Starting Indie Builder's Catalog price for you: **$429 shipped direct (limit 2 drivetrains, or 1 AWD)**
* Best Indie Builder's Catalog price for you, in volume: **$407 shipped direct**

...and because we have been asked this question about a hundred times:

Yes, the Lofty AWD option that includes (4) 90 MM wheels will cost less than the TB DD dual, without wheels.  This is not an endorsement.

We've done the hard part and pre-negotiated small-volume discounts, in Mandarin, direct with the manufacturer, for our Indie Builder community.

This means, if any of you would like to run a small Indiegogo with Lofty for 30 AWD Lofty drivetrains and put them on @Eboosted Sector 9 Bintangs, all that's standing between you and glory is hard work.

Or, go big and design a new drop-through deck of your own that Lofty manufactures in qty 100. and launch your Indiegogo with backercamp.com and push the industry forward.  If Dualomo can do it based on the Bustin Newsletter mailing list, any of you certainly can, too.

I want to thank everyone who's helped encourage and/or goad us into negotiating with Lofty, for the community.  @DAddYE @BillGordon and @esk8jpn, thanks for your pioneering spirit, you set the bar for us all.   

Special thanks to those who spent personal time and weekends negotiating with a Chinese supplier for zero financial benefit, and of course, to the Lofty customers who are testing and sharing information with our community: thank you, @mishrasubhransu @sofu and @Winfly.
 
We'll post the Lofty Indie Builder's Price Book later today.  By the way, if you guys think this is dope, let us know below.  

The hardest part for the Western startup entrepeneur is finding and selecting the right Asian suppliers, and we're considering opening up new suppliers as we move forward, together.  Thanks team.
```

## \#1079 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-05-01T02:52:22.054Z Reads: 230

```
58(rpm/volts)\*42(volts)\*3.14\*90mm/60sec = 11473mm/sec = 41km/hr = 25.6mph

Of course battery resistance and motor winding resistance will bring this speed down.
```

---
## \#1080 Posted by: Pedrodemio Posted at: 2019-05-01T02:59:11.541Z Reads: 232

Just keep in mind that this will almost never be reached, if you consider sag and that we stay for little time at full voltage, the average speed of the board will be much lower
```

## \#1121 Posted by: gmurad Posted at: 2019-05-02T20:22:11.547Z Reads: 226

```
I think the scrutiny here is warranted (A lot of early confusion around the KV and some conflicting reports of the performance) and the disappointment is to be expected (Everyone wants a DD, specially one that is cheap and early on this had promise). 
I remember earlier in the thread @Touch415 was being very real about the performance and he was met with some resistance

Someone should do a Summary of the DD so people know what to expect. The info I can add:

At **56KV**...
*(According to the calculator that is spot on for me on belt driven systems)*
- Top speed with 10s and 90mm (eLofty) wheels: [18.06 mph - 29.07 km/h](http://calc.esk8.it/#{%22batt-type-lipo%22:0,%22batt-cells%22:10,%22motor-kv%22:56,%22system-efficiency%22:85,%22motor-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-size%22:90}|)
- Top speed with 12s and 90mm (eLofty) wheels: [21.68 mph - 34.88 km/h](http://calc.esk8.it/#{%22batt-type-lipo%22:0,%22batt-cells%22:12,%22motor-kv%22:56,%22system-efficiency%22:85,%22motor-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-size%22:90}|)
- Top speed with 10s and 110mm(TB Wheel) wheels: [22.08 mph - 35.53 km/h](http://calc.esk8.it/#{%22batt-type-lipo%22:0,%22batt-cells%22:10,%22motor-kv%22:56,%22system-efficiency%22:85,%22motor-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-size%22:110}|)
- Top speed with 12s and 110mm(TB Wheel) wheels: [26.49 mph - 42.64 km/h](http://calc.esk8.it/#{%22batt-type-lipo%22:0,%22batt-cells%22:12,%22motor-kv%22:56,%22system-efficiency%22:85,%22motor-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-size%22:110}|)
- Top speed with 10s and 147mm(e.g.: Bergmeister size) wheels: [29.5 mph - 47.48 km/h](http://calc.esk8.it/#{%22batt-type-lipo%22:0,%22batt-cells%22:10,%22motor-kv%22:56,%22system-efficiency%22:85,%22motor-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-size%22:147}|)
- Top speed with 12s and 147mm(e.g.: Bergmeister size) wheels: [35.4 mph - 56.98 km/h](http://calc.esk8.it/#{%22batt-type-lipo%22:0,%22batt-cells%22:12,%22motor-kv%22:56,%22system-efficiency%22:85,%22motor-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-pulley-teeth%22:1,%22wheel-size%22:147}|)


DD is **DKP** only which by can be converted into TKP by removing the middle piece. RKP is the more common truck style used in e-skates. There are only pulleys for Kegel core (no ABEC11)
```

## \#1168 Posted by: BillGordon Posted at: 2019-05-16T18:55:21.000Z Reads: 223

```
So I just did a series of speed tests with the following setup:

Board:

1st gen eLofty DD 

Diyeboard 4-speed esc/remote in 4TH GEAR BABY! 

10s2p Sanyo

TB 110 wheels 

Single hairless Malibu barbie duct-taped on front 


Rider:

6'3" (I'm a great wind screen) 

225 lbs

Male chastity belt with Touch 'n Tell LED warning lights


Data according to GPS Trip Tracker app:

Highest speed: 23.1 mph

Highest speed easily maintained and held: 22.5 mph

Not blazing fast, but enough to pull away from a turgid and lubed-up @Brenternet on foot, and that's my only real need/concern.

Plenty for me, especially given the official speed limits where I live. I'm not in a situation where I can hit 30-35 and expect to keep my board. Well, that and the fact that I'm a little sissy boy with perpetually moist undie fronts.

Hills are no problem whatsoever, and I still love the ride I get from the smooth power delivery, wide stance, and the TB 110s. 

Easily the best esk8 purchase I've ever made.
```
